## 2026-07-11 22:59 — kiro-cli
- Action: Implemented worktree-per-CLI dispatch per handoff 202607111550-dispatcher-worktree-per-cli (ADR-0004 amendment). Every dispatched CLI now runs inside its OWN git worktree (`.wt/<project>/<cli>/`, reusing scripts/wt-bootstrap.sh — no second worktree implementation) instead of the shared primary checkout; worktree-creation failure fails the dispatch outright (handoff stays OPEN, dispatch-failure report written, NO fallback to the primary checkout — enforced by construction, not comment). Each dispatch also cuts (or reuses) a per-handoff branch `exec/<cli>/<slug>` from a DECLARED base (`origin/master`, or a handoff's optional `Base:` field), never from ambient HEAD — the second, independent defect the ADR amendment named (Kimi-off-Kiro's-branch is possible even with worktrees). Old `cd "$root"` shared-checkout invocation is fully removed from the dispatch path (grep confirms zero matches).
- Files: .ai/tools/dispatch-handoffs.sh (added ensure_cli_worktree, ensure_declared_base_branch, base_for, worktree_path_for; exec block rewired); .ai/tests/test-dispatch-worktree.sh (new, 24/24); docs/architecture/0004-worktree-multi-project-topology.md (Follow-ups updated — struck the now-false "unchanged, still runs cd $root" sentence, documented the new .ai-junction git-status finding).
- Decisions: Found and worked around a genuine, separate latent bug while building the dirty-worktree safety check: `git status` does NOT respect `.git/info/exclude` for files added under a Windows directory-JUNCTION after creation — it recurses through the reparse point and reports new `.ai/handoffs/**` files as untracked (`?? .ai/handoffs/...`) even though `wt-bootstrap.sh` writes the `.ai` exclude line correctly. This made every dispatch spuriously trip the "worktree has uncommitted changes, reuse-as-is" safety path (since `.ai/` legitimately churns constantly). Fix: scoped the dirty-check to exclude `.ai/` paths specifically (`grep -v ' \.ai/'` on `git status --porcelain` output) rather than touching wt-bootstrap.sh's exclude mechanism — that mechanism is explicitly out of scope per the handoff's NON-goal (the activity-log/junction race is tracked separately). Documented as a new Follow-up in the ADR rather than silently patched over. Committed locally on exec/kiro/dispatcher-worktree (cut from origin/master) — did NOT push or open a PR (no verified network/gh access in this session); left as an explicit next step in the handoff's completion report. Full grep-verified evidence, test output, and the concurrent-dispatch proof are pasted in .ai/handoffs/to-kiro/done/202607111550-dispatcher-worktree-per-cli.md.

## 2026-07-11 22:43 — claude-code
- Action: RESCUE-AND-LAND of the §14 rollout after a shared-worktree race, then merged PR #39 (575b5af) + PR #40 (8fd7006) to master (owner-gated Tier C). THE RACE: the Kimi and Kiro §14 sync handoffs were dispatched CONCURRENTLY into the SAME working tree. Both executors did `git checkout -b <their>/sync-operating-prompt-s14` in that one shared worktree, so the second checkout swapped the branch out from under the first. Kimi committed 4c924ec (.kimi + .kiro steering) and Kiro committed 07d97dc (.kiro steering) onto DIVERGENT branches; only Kiro's branch reached origin, and the working tree ended up on a branch whose .kimi replica was not the one Kimi had authored. check-ssot-drift.sh flagged it — the gate did its job. NOTHING WAS LOST: Kimi's commit was byte-identical to the SSOT-derived replica (all six replica blobs and master's principles.md are literally the SAME git object, 6cbd073), it simply was not checked out at the moment the drift ran. RECONCILIATION: rather than re-run the two handoffs, I cherry-picked the surviving replica content onto claude/operating-prompt-s14 (PR #40), which already carried the SSOT §14, so one branch landed SSOT + all four replicas atomically. Post-merge master: check-ssot-drift.sh = "Checked: 24 replicas, Drift: 0"; §14 present at line 212 in .ai/instructions, .kimi/steering, .kiro/steering; all four log entries (14:45, 15:35 claude-code; 22:24 kimi-cli; 22:29 kiro-cli) intact. 4ai-panes suites on merged master: selector-e2e 81/0, pane-runner 37/0, pane-supervisor 9/0 (the known case-C timing flake did NOT trip; single clean run, no rerun needed). Branch cleanup done — see Files.
- Files: master @ 8fd7006. Merges: 575b5af (#39), 8fd7006 (#40). Added 1e21bb0 (tools/multi-cli-install/package.json 0.0.19 -> 0.0.20). Deleted branches: kimi/sync-operating-prompt-s14 (local; never had a remote), kiro/sync-operating-prompt-s14 (local+remote), claude/pane-pacing-and-src-badge (local+remote), claude/operating-prompt-s14 (REMOTE ONLY — local retained, see Decisions). This entry: .ai/activity/log.md.
- Decisions: THE SURVIVAL OF ALL THREE LOG ENTRIES WAS LUCK, NOT DESIGN. The three commits happened to touch disjoint files (.kimi vs .kiro vs the SSOT), so the racing checkouts could not clobber each other's content; had two CLIs written the SAME file — or had either appended to .ai/activity/log.md, which EVERY CLI writes to — the loser's work would have been silently destroyed with no gate to catch it. The drift gate caught the symptom (a replica out of sync) only because §14 has a checkable SSOT; a lost activity-log entry has no such gate and would simply be gone. Treat today's clean outcome as a near-miss, not a validation of the current dispatch model. The durable fix — worktree-per-CLI (each executor gets its own checkout, so a branch checkout cannot be observed by another CLI) — is owner-approved and IN FLIGHT in docs/architecture/0004-worktree-multi-project-topology.md; until it lands, do NOT dispatch concurrent handoffs that touch the same tree. CAUGHT ON THE WAY IN: PR #40 was RED on the `gates` check (check-version-bump.sh) and GitHub would have let me merge it anyway — mergeStateStatus was UNSTABLE, not BLOCKED, i.e. the version gate is NOT a required check. #40 changed versioned framework content (.ai/instructions, .claude, .kimi, .kiro, .opencode, CLAUDE.md) without bumping tools/multi-cli-install/package.json, which is precisely the hole that script exists to close: no bump -> onboarded projects still match the template version -> the drift warning stays silent -> §14 ships to NOBODY. I did not override it; I merged master into the branch and bumped 0.0.19 -> 0.0.20 (1e21bb0) so §14 gets its own version, then merged green. FOLLOW-UPS: (1) make `gates` a REQUIRED check — a version gate that a merge can walk past is decoration; (2) check-version-bump.sh only tests `old != new`, so a version DOWNGRADE passes it; (3) local branch claude/operating-prompt-s14 was NOT deleted because it is checked out in the shared worktree where another CLI currently holds ~152 uncommitted lines of the worktree-topology ADR — deleting it meant yanking the branch out from under a live agent, i.e. re-running the exact race this entry documents; delete it once that work lands. Its remote is gone and its content is fully in master.

## 2026-07-10 14:20 — claude-code
- Action: Fixed a pane-runner crash that stopped the kimi self-drive pane after one handoff (owner-reported). Root cause (debugger, repro-confirmed): pane-runner.ps1 sets $ErrorActionPreference='Stop', and $script:InvokeCli runs `Invoke-Expression $cmd 2>&1 | Out-Host` — under Stop, a native CLI's stderr line merged via 2>&1 is promoted to a terminating NativeCommandError. Kimi streams progress to stderr, so its first line threw, unwound the finally blocks ("pane-runner stopped - claim released"), and exited the whole supervisor loop → no more polling, handoff 202607100655 left OPEN. Fix: force EAP='Continue' around ONLY the native invoke (restore in finally; loses no signal — continue/done is decided by Test-HandoffDone, not exit/stderr) + guarded UTF-8 console encoding (fixes the `•`→ÔÇó mojibake). test-pane-runner.ps1 17/17 pass; focused regression proves real InvokeCli survives a stderr child + preserves exit code. Committed ecc5568, pushed, then re-synced live install via scripts/sync-4ai-panes-install.ps1 (first real non-no-op copy: pane-runner.ps1 + README.md drifted→copied, SHA256 MATCH, install parses).
- Files: tools/4ai-panes/pane-runner.ps1 (ecc5568); re-synced ~/.rwn-auto/rwn-4AI-panes/{pane-runner.ps1,README.md}
- Decisions: Bug was in the CLI-invocation core the unit tests mock over, so it evaded coverage — flagged. Same class not present in the interactive escape hatch (no 2>&1 merge) or dispatch-handoffs.sh (bash). Handoff 202607100655 (Kimi MCP cleanup) is still OPEN — relaunching the kimi pane on the fixed runner will now pick it up and poll.

# Activity Log

Newest entries at the top. Each CLI prepends an entry after completing substantive work.

**Timestamp rule:** the `HH:MM` in each entry heading is local wall-clock time at the
moment of prepending (i.e. when the work finished, not when it started). CLIs on
different local clocks may produce timestamps that don't sort monotonically;
**prepend order is the authoritative sequencing**, timestamps are annotations.

**Archive:** older entries live in `.ai/activity/archive/YYYY-MM.md` (one file per
calendar month, entries grouped by day). AI CLIs do not auto-read the archive; only
consulted when the user explicitly references historical activity. See
`.ai/activity/archive/README.md` for the archival protocol.

See the AI contract in this project's CLI steering files (`CLAUDE.md`,
`.kimi/steering/00-ai-contract.md`, `.kiro/steering/00-ai-contract.md`) for format and rules.

---

## 2026-07-09 18:40 — claude-code
- Action: OpenCode frictionless-by-default (owner directive). Changed `opencode.json` permission `edit`/`bash` from `ask` → `allow` so OpenCode stops prompting per-tool during deploy/automation work. SAFE because OpenCode's enforcement is the `.opencode/plugin/framework-guard.js` plugin, which fires on `tool.execute.before` INDEPENDENT of the permission prompt (proven 2026-07-09 task 7/10) — so `allow` removes friction without removing the mechanical guard; the git backstop (ADR-0005) sits behind it. Tradeoff (accepted by owner): loses the human-prompt last-resort backstop for OpenCode only. Folded a live "guard-still-works under allow" negative probe into the pending deploy brief (202607091745) so the next OpenCode run proves the plugin still blocks an out-of-lane write.

- Decisions: OpenCode is uniquely safe to auto-approve (unlike Kimi `--yolo`/Kiro `--trust-all-tools`, which DISABLE their hooks) because its guard is a plugin, not a permission-gated hook — reinforces ADR-0007. Used POSIX-relative path normalization invariant (no `/` prefix, no `\\`, no drive letters) so Windows tests would pass without constructing fake Windows inputs. Released as `v0.0.3` (minor version since this adds genuinely new module surface — `src/upgrade/`).

## 2026-05-28 — claude-code (orchestrator)
- Action: Closed the v0.0.2-pre.4 "SHA divergence" forensic question flagged in the previous entry. Infra-engineer ran read-only git diagnostics: the tag is healthy and was never divergent. The two SHAs ("local 993dc49 vs remote 2120ce3") are different layers of the SAME annotated tag — `2120ce3` is the tag-object SHA (annotated tags are git objects with their own SHA containing tagger + message + commit pointer), `993dc49` is the wrapped commit SHA. `git cat-file -t v0.0.2-pre.4` → `tag` confirms annotated. `git rev-parse v0.0.2-pre.4^{}` → `993dc49` (peeled commit matches `git log`). Both local and remote refs/tags/v0.0.2-pre.4 resolve to `2120ce3` (identical). GitHub release for pre.4 was created cleanly on 2026-04-29 at 12:13:48Z, workflow ran on 993dc49, succeeded 5s later — no force-push, no clobber, no problem. The pre.5 release cycle was technically unnecessary work caused by my naive SHA comparison (commit-SHA vs tag-object-SHA without peeling). Added a new known-limitations entry "Annotated tag SHA comparisons — peel before diffing" documenting the trap + correct mitigation (check `git cat-file -t <tag>` first, peel with `^{}` for annotated tags before comparing).
- Grep-verified evidence:
  - Tag is annotated: `git cat-file -t v0.0.2-pre.4` → `tag` (per infra-engineer)
  - Peeled commit matches master: `git rev-parse v0.0.2-pre.4^{}` → `993dc49`
  - Known-limitations entry exists: `rg -c "Annotated tag SHA comparisons" .ai/known-limitations.md` → `1`
- Files: `.ai/known-limitations.md` (+~50 lines new section), `.ai/activity/log.md` (this entry).
- Decisions: Logged in known-limitations rather than baking into release-engineer agent definition — false-alarm pattern is rare enough that the searchable lesson-log is the right resting place; baking into agent prompt would add prompt weight for a once-in-many-cycles concern. Did NOT redact/correct the previous pre.5 entry's "divergence" language — the entry accurately reflects what I believed at the time; layering this entry on top preserves the diagnostic history (and is itself a small case study in why self-grep-verify matters — I had `git cat-file` available and didn't run it before passing the alarm through).

## 2026-04-29 — claude-code (orchestrator)
- Action: User asked whether to npm publish v0.0.1. Surfaced the case against — five concrete risks: (1) reorganize-mode never run on a real codebase, fixtures don't have real imports/configs to break; (2) published-package layout untested (`npm pack` + `npm install -g <tarball>` never run, B3 bundled-assets resolver only verified in dev mode where `assets/` is present, not in published-mode where it's bundled into the tarball); (3) squatting npm name with buggy v0.0.1 is worse than not having it — reputation damage transfers permanently to v1.0.0; (4) no support story (no CHANGELOG, no migration guide, no "report a bug" pointer); (5) narrow undo path — npm allows unpublish in 72h but versions can never be re-used, so panic-unpublish burns v0.0.1 forever. Recommended the conservative path: hold, GitHub Release stays the only distribution channel until real-project validation gate clears (per locked policy in `.ai/known-limitations.md`). Did NOT amend `.ai/known-limitations.md` to add the 5 risks I surfaced — they're orchestrator-time analysis, not new project-level limitations; the existing fixture-only-validation entry already covers the structural risk. Did NOT modify the locked policy text — re-affirmed. The right time to revisit is after at least one real-project validation comes back clean. Note for future me: "Hold" doesn't mean "never" — it means "not yet, with a clear unblock condition." When a user has a real project to validate against, that triggers the unblock review.

- Decisions: Fixed Claude's hook rather than handoff-bouncing — the `input=$(cat)` + `echo | python` pattern was silently failing on Windows bash inside `$()`, causing all 15 write-edit + bash guard tests to fail. The `python3 || python || echo ""` fallback (used by Kimi/Kiro hooks) works because `python3` (App Execution Alias on Windows) fails without consuming stdin, allowing `python` to read from the preserved pipeline. This is a platform quirk worth documenting for future hook authors.

## 2026-04-21 11:15 — claude-code (orchestrator)
- Action: Fixed the `rm -rf /` false-positive destructive-cmd guard surfaced during new-project.sh test cleanup. Pattern `*"rm -rf /"*` was matching any command containing `rm -rf /` as substring (e.g. `rm -rf /tmp/foo`). Delegated to infra-engineer: chose bash regex approach over 40-pattern case expansion — regex uses 3 named sub-patterns (`rm_flags`, `rm_target`, `rm_tail`) that require a shell-boundary (space/`;`/`&`/`|`/EOL) after the target. `.claude/hooks/pretool-bash.sh` patched; `.claude/hooks/test_hooks.sh` gained 4 new tests (t18–t21): `rm -rf /tmp/foo` → allow (was blocked), `rm -rf / ` → block, `rm -rf /;echo ok` → block (separator boundary), `rm -rf /usr` → allow. Ad-hoc verified: `rm -rf ~/foo`, `rm -rf *.log`, `rm -rf ./build`, `sudo rm -rf /var/log` correctly allow; `rm -rf ~`, `rm -rf *`, `rm -rf .`, `rm -fr /`, `rm -r -f /`, `rm --recursive --force /` correctly block. Test count 17→21, PASS 21/21. Parity handoffs dispatched: to-kimi and to-kiro both at `202604211100-fix-rm-rf-false-positive.md` with the same bug spec + suggested fix patterns + 4 new test cases. 3 commits pushed: `84b4f72` (Claude fix), `00e7156` (Kimi handoff), `16aa502` (Kiro handoff). All in origin/master at `29000b7..16aa502`.
- Files: .claude/hooks/pretool-bash.sh (regex replace), .claude/hooks/test_hooks.sh (+4 tests); 2 new handoffs in to-kimi/open/ + to-kiro/open/; 3 commits on origin/master
- Decisions: Regex over case-pattern — 3 named sub-patterns read like a spec, 40-pattern case would be hard to audit for coverage gaps. Kept the conservative `echo rm -rf /` still-blocks behavior (literal-string echo gets flagged) — pre-fix behavior, not worth refining this pass since it's conservative rather than dangerous. Didn't touch the `~`, `*`, `.` target variants (all got boundary-required in the regex by construction — no separate fix needed). Kiro's handoff body is Kiro-style since their guard normalizes to lowercase first — same bug logic, slightly different hook shape; asked Kiro to adapt the regex to their implementation. Session remaining open items after this: file the 2 pre-filled bug issues (user action only), ship a real feature (user initiative).

Three delegated-to-infra-engineer steps: (1) captured `kiro --version` (0.11.130), filled the `<FILL IN>` placeholder + added a `Filed:` field to the report; (2) URL-encoded the report body into a pre-filled GitHub issue URL at `https://github.com/kirodotdev/Kiro/issues/new?title=...&body=...` saved to `.ai/reports/kiro-bug-prefilled-issue-url.txt`; (3) reformatted the body to match Kiro's standard issue template (Description / Reproduction steps / Expected / Actual / Environment / Additional context) per user guidance, regenerated URL (6222 bytes, no truncation). **Hook worked in practice** — infra-engineer's initial inline bash encoding attempt was blocked by the destructive-cmd-guard because the body contains the literal `rm -rf /` string (describing the threat model). Workaround: created `scripts/gen-kiro-issue-url.py` — deterministic re-encoding when the report changes. 3 commits pushed: `6aa1ee1` (version fill), `f573736` (initial URL), `c8a2d44` (template-aligned body + regen URL + Python helper). - Files: .ai/reports/kiro-bug-subagent-hook-inheritance.md (edit), .ai/reports/kiro-bug-prefilled-issue-url.txt (new then updated), scripts/gen-kiro-issue-url.py (new); 3 commits on origin/master
- Decisions: Reformatted to template-aligned structure rather than keeping original sections, but kept the original structured content in the report file above the template-aligned block (framework readers benefit from the richer structure; GitHub issue readers get the templated version). Added Python URL-encoding helper as side effect — worth keeping because the report will likely be re-filed or amended and re-encoding is non-trivial without a script. Hook block on `rm -rf /` substring was a real positive — destructive-cmd-guard was supposed to catch bash commands containing that, and it did, even when the intent was a benign URL encoding. Worth noting as a future UX concern: the hook can't distinguish "I am literally running rm -rf /" from "I am echoing/encoding a string that contains rm -rf /". Not fixing this session — documented for future. Session state at close: framework work complete, user's final Kiro-bug action is one click on the URL in .ai/reports/kiro-bug-prefilled-issue-url.txt.

## 2026-04-17 21:35 — claude-code
- Action: Executed handoff `to-claude/010-project-structure-root-policy.md` from kiro-cli. (1) Added a "Root file policy" section to `.claude/agents/orchestrator.md` — only `AGENTS.md`, `README.md`, `CLAUDE.md` at root; every other kind mapped to a directory (src/, tests/, docs/, infra/, migrations/, scripts/, tools/, config/, assets/); framework dirs exempt by `.`-prefix. Included an explicit exception-handling clause: subagents that hit tooling constraints requiring root files (`.gitignore`, `.github/workflows/`, etc.) surface the exception to orchestrator for user approval rather than silently placing root files. (2) Rewrote `.claude/agents/infra-engineer.md` write scope around the new `infra/**` layout (docker/, terraform/, k8s/, ci/) with tooling-required root exceptions (`.github/workflows/`, `Dockerfile` when build chain needs it, etc.) called out explicitly as "raise before using." Also enumerated what infra-engineer explicitly does NOT touch now that src/, tests/, docs/, migrations/, config/, assets/ exist as distinct dirs. (3) Item 1 of the handoff (docs/ resource) was already done in handoff 009 — noted in the handoff's DONE annotation.
- Files: .claude/agents/orchestrator.md (edit), .claude/agents/infra-engineer.md (edit), .ai/handoffs/to-claude/open/010-project-structure-root-policy.md (status→DONE inline; left in open/ for kiro-cli to validate + move)
- Decisions: Executed the root-file policy as written but built in exception-handling rather than pretending it's absolute. Several real tooling constraints force root-level files that no subagent can override — git needs `.gitignore` at root (or zero gitignore), GitHub Actions needs `.github/workflows/` at root, and build tools (npm/pyproject/Cargo/go) need their manifests at root unless the whole build chain is configured to look elsewhere (and some, like `go mod`, have no override). Rather than have the orchestrator block every legitimate root-file creation, the policy treats them as "exceptions requiring explicit user approval" and directs that approved exceptions get documented in `docs/architecture/` or `docs/standards/`. This keeps the policy's intent (minimize root clutter, clear directory ownership) while letting the project actually ship. Did not update other subagents' write scopes this turn — coder/tester/doc-writer/etc. already operate within the new directory structure once they know src/, tests/, etc. are the canonical locations (which the orchestrator's delegation brief will include). If specific subagents hit path issues in practice, I'll edit them per-case.

## 2026-04-17 20:55 — claude-code
- Action: Reviewed the proposed `project/` directory-structure per handoff `to-claude/008-review-project-structure.md` from kiro-cli. Wrote feedback to `.ai/research/project-structure-feedback-claude.md` — agreed with intent (clear product boundary + simpler agent scopes, framework dirs stay outside), pushed back against the `project/` wrapper mechanism. Main concerns: (1) tooling expects canonical paths at repo root (package.json, pyproject.toml, Dockerfile, .github/workflows/, etc.) — wrapping in `project/` forces per-tool cwd juggling indefinitely; (2) CHANGELOG / manifests create "is it product or meta?" ambiguity that breaks the "one boundary" promise; (3) repo looks like a monorepo pattern without the monorepo benefits. Proposed an alternative: keep everything at root, convert subagent scopes from negative-filtered ("anywhere except framework dirs") to positive-allowlists ("only `src/**`, `tests/**`, etc.") — captures the real benefit (scope simplification) without the cost (tooling friction).
- Files: .ai/research/project-structure-feedback-claude.md (new), .ai/handoffs/to-claude/open/008-review-project-structure.md (status→DONE inline; left in open/ for kiro-cli to validate + move)
- Decisions: Held back from vetoing — if user chooses `project/`, Claude-side migration is ~30 min of system-prompt edits across 10 subagents and is not a blocker. Just flagged that the recurring tooling tax (every `npm`/`pytest`/`docker build` invocation needing wrapper cwd handling, every IDE project-root override, every CI workflow needing path adjustments) doesn't go away after migration — it's ongoing. The alternative (positive-allowlist scopes at root) captures the proposal's stated benefit (agent scope clarity) for free.
